              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 The Brutalism Appreciation Society
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 As they start to disappear from our towns and cities, this group is for anyone who appreciates buildings built in this much maligned architectural style. Consider Brutalism as architecture in the raw, with an emphasis on materials, textures and construction, producing highly expressive forms. Seen in the work of Le Corbusier from the late 1940s with the Unite d’Habitation in Marseilles, the term Brutalism was first used in England by the architectural historian Reyner Banham. In 1954 it referred to the work of Alison and Peter Smithson’s school at Hunstanton in Norfolk because of its uncompromising approach to the display of structure and services, albeit in a steel building rather than reinforced concrete. Also called New Brutalism, it encouraged the use of beton brut (raw concrete), in which patterns created by wooden shuttering are replicated through boardmarking, as can be seen in the work of Denys Lasdun, or where the aggregate is bush or pick-hammered, as at the Barbican Estate in London. Scale was important and the style is characterised by massive concrete shapes colliding abruptly, while service ducts and ventilation towers are overtly displayed. Brutalist building materials include brick, glass, steel, rough-hewn stone, and gabions. Conversely, not all buildings exhibiting an exposed concrete exterior can be considered Brutalist. What to look for in a Brutalist building: 1. Rough unfinished surfaces 2. Unusual shapes 3. Heavy-looking materials 4. Massive forms 5. Small windows in relation to the other parts For further reference:- http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brutalist_architecture http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_brutalist_structures 
                </div>
               </div>
               <div>
                <div class="_8um4">
                 <span class="_8ul_"><i class="_8wo5 _8wos img sp_oDRLRzjLfgY sx_8f3bf5"></i><span class="_8um1">12&nbsp;万位成员</span></span><span class="_8um0"><i class="_8wo6 _8wos img sp_oDRLRzjLfgY sx_ce40e2"></i><span class="_8um2">39 篇新帖</span></span>
                </div>
               </div>

                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Bauhaus Design
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 The influence of the Bauhaus on design education was significant. One of the main objectives of the Bauhaus was to unify art, craft, and technology, and this approach was incorporated into the curriculum of the Bauhaus. The structure of the Bauhaus Vorkurs (preliminary course) reflected a pragmatic approach to integrating theory and application. In their first year, students learnt the basic elements and principles of design and colour theory, and experimented with a range of materials and processes. This approach to design education became a common feature of architectural and design school in many countries. For example, the Shillito Design School in Sydney stands as a unique link between Australia and the Bauhaus. The colour and design syllabus of the Shillito Design School was firmly underpinned by the theories and ideologies of the Bauhaus. Its first year foundational course mimicked the Vorkurs and focused on the elements and principles of design plus colour theory and application. The founder of the school, Phyllis Shillito, which opened in 1962 and closed in 1980, firmly believed that "A student who has mastered the basic principles of design, can design anything from a dress to a kitchen stove
                </div>
               </div>
               <div>
                <div class="_8um4">
                 <span class="_8ul_"><i class="_8wo5 _8wos img sp_oDRLRzjLfgY sx_8f3bf5"></i><span class="_8um1">1.6&nbsp;万位成员</span></span><span class="_8um0"><i class="_8wo6 _8wos img sp_oDRLRzjLfgY sx_ce40e2"></i><span class="_8um2">0 篇新帖</span></span>

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 MYSTERY OF WATERCOLOUR
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 We welcome you to solve the vibrant mystery which no matter how hard you try, becomes more thrilling and challenging with every single effort or say, the mystery which has wheels within wheels- "The Mystery Of Watercolour". No longer stigmatized as only a 'sketch' medium, serious artists are constantly pushing the boundaries of what watercolor can be. A rapidly executed watercolor thrills with its immediacy, energy and sheer boldness. And hence, we provide the master as well as the learner watercolourists from all around the globe, a Dias to showcase their work as well as learn and traverse this hypnotic master medium- Watercolour. We have laid down certain guidelines and tip-offs to ensure the smooth working of the group: __________________________________________________________ 1. Do create whatever moves you and as much as you can using the watercolour medium only. Works based on other mediums will be removed from the group. 2. Do learn from the masters and accept brickbats in an optimistic manner. 3. Do like and give your valuable feedback on the feats of other artists. We appreciate fault-findings or carpings to be done in a pragmatic way. 4. Do mention the paper details(Size and Type) and also let us know about any new expertis8e used in your paintings which would help us to expand our knowledge about the medium further. 5. Do mention the painter's name in case you tend to share somebody else's work so as to avoid misconceptions (charges of plagiarism). 6. Do report if you notice any kind of 'not right' thing taking place. 6. Do appreciate as well as acknowledge. Praising anybody for his or her task can increase the confidence of the receiver. Last but not the least, we aim to encourage the learning of this living language, with grammars and nuances that challenge us beyond any other intellectual or creative pursuit one ever experiences. You may kindly revert for furtherance at mysteryofwatercolour@gmail.com Thank you. 
                </div>

              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Urbanism
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 The group for the fans of the clear division between the city and the country. For creating the coherent cities and to protect the open landscape and natural environment. Modernism sought to expand the urban realm into the rural area, compromising the urban/rural divide. But these days we want to reverse that strategy by expanding the rural into the city (i.e. introducing urban roof gardens, urban farming, tree lined streets, etc..) and thus improving the quality of life. To get the proper living conditions for people now, and for creating the sustainable environment in the future. Another important issue is bringing out genius loci, by protecting and continuing the local traditions of urban planning and architecture. To avoid the unification as a direct consequence of globalisation. The local marketing bases on looking for unique values. Continuing the tradition allows to profit of methods which have been developed through ages and thus suits the local conditions and communities in the proper way. The group addressee are citizens, this shouldn't be only a hermetic and scientific place. Although we do not want to ignore the current research results. What accompanies the creation of this group is the strong believe that when a place belongs to somebody - or to a group of people - it becomes neat, ordered, well managed and friendly. It becomes a good place to live. There is a simple condition of belonging (not necessary being ones property). The place belongs to an individual and a group of people in case when it may be influenced by them. This group is open to all. Yet it is strictly limited to topics (essays, conferences, books, interviews, and so forth) related to Urbanism (including urban planning, sustainability as the tags mention). We do not accept any self-promotion, or topics off Urbanism (architecture [buildings], or photography…). Please accept our guidelines before posting in the group. The Netiquette is obligation - please refer to http://www.albion.com/netiquette/corerules.html Thank you
                </div>
               </div>

                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 :: ART BASEL :: MIAMI BEACH :: FANS CLUB ::
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 PICTURES OF THE :: ART BASEL :: ART SHOW IN MIAMI BEACH Since 2004, Sylvie Robert took Over2000 pictures during the Art Basel Miami Beach the most important art show in the United States - a cultural and social highlight for the Americas. As the sister event of Switzerland's Art Basel, the most prestigious art show worldwide for the past 39 years, Art Basel Miami Beach combines an international selection of top galleries with an exciting program of special exhibitions, parties and crossover events featuring music, film, architecture and design. Exhibition sites are located in the city's beautiful Art Deco District, within walking distance of the beach and many hotels. An exclusive selection of more than 220 leading art galleries from North America, Latin America, Europe, Asia and Africa will exhibit 20th and 21st century artworks by over 2,000 artists. The exhibiting galleries are among the world's most respected art dealers, offering exceptional pieces by both renowned artists and cutting-edge newcomers. Special exhibition sections feature young galleries, performance art, public art projects and video art. The show will be a vital source for art lovers, allowing them to both discover new developments in contemporary art and experience rare museum-calibre artworks. INVITE YOUR FRIENDS: All you have to do to help is this: ► 1 Join this group. ► 2 Click on "Invite People to Join" button in the right menu. ► 3 Select all of your friends. ► 4 Click on the "Send invitation" button And you're done!

              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 The Ziegfeld Follies Club {Tribute to the Ziegfeld Girls &amp; Other Follies}
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Welcome to the Ziegfeld Follies Club! A Tribute to the Ziegfeld Girls, this group covers the entertainers of the Ziegfeld Follies, the photographs of Ziegfeld's Photographer Alfred Cheney Johnston, George White's Scandals, and entertainers and dancers of the Folies Bergère, Paris, The Casino de Paris, Moulin Rogue, the Radio City Rockettes and the British Tiller Girls, Earl Carroll's Vanities, other old Broadway acts, &amp; vintage show girls, European and American. GROUP RULES {PLEASE READ} *.Please be respectful in your comments, the Ziegfeld Girls etc have living friends, relatives, and Grandchildren and Great Grandchildren in this group. *. Refrain from selling anything, it will be removed. *. No posting photos of stage items, ie costume pieces bought off or shown on the internet stating they are vintage "Ziegfeld". Or links to the selling of these fraudulently labeled items. We will remove the post without warning. *. No full frontal nudity, (Bare Breasts) etc, these photos and comments will be removed without question. We comply with facebook guidelines regarding this issue. *If a post is not related in any way to group description. ie, {modern photos replicating Alfred Cheney Johnston's Ziegfeld Girl Photos}. They will be removed without warning. * The admins reserve the right to ban members for not complying with these rules. Thanks! *The Ziegfeld Follies, elaborate theatrical productions on Broadway in New York City from 1907 to 1931. Inspired by the Folies Bergère of Paris, the Ziegfeld Follies were conceived and mounted by Florenz Ziegfeld, at the suggestion of the entertainer Anna Held. *George White's Scandals, a long-running string of Broadway revues produced by George White from 1919–1939, modeled after the Ziegfeld Follies. *Earl Carroll's Vanities, Carroll produced &amp; directed numerous Broadway musicals, famous for featuring the most lightly clad showgirls on Broadway. *The Folies Bergère, cabaret music hall, Paris, France. Est. 1869, at the height of its fame and popularity from the 1890s' Belle Époque through the 1920s. The American Ziegfeld Follies were based on these shows. *Casino de Paris, one of the well known music halls of Paris, with a history dating back to the 18th century. *Moulin Rouge, best known as the spiritual birthplace of the modern form of the can-can dance. *Radio City Rockettes The group first kicked to life in 1925 as the "Missouri Rockets," creator, Russell Markert said "I had seen the John Tiller girls in the Ziegfeld Follies of 1922,""If I ever got a chance to get a group of American girls who would be taller and have longer legs and could do really complicated tap routines and eye-high kicks … they'd knock your socks off!" *The Tiller Girls were among the most popular dance troupes of the 1900s, first formed by John Tiller in Manchester, England, in 1890. 
                </div>
               </div>

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 ABSTRACT EXPRESSIONISM 
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Abstract expressionism is an American post–World War II art movement in American painting, developed in New York in the 1940s.[1] It was the first specifically American movement to achieve international influence and put New York City at the center of the western art world, a role formerly filled by Paris. Although the term "abstract expressionism" was first applied to American art in 1946 by the art critic Robert Coates, it had been first used in Germany in 1919 in the magazine Der Sturm, regarding German Expressionism. In the United States, Alfred Barr was the first to use this term in 1929 in relation to works by Wassily Kandinsky.[2] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstract_expressionism
                </div>
               </div>

              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Plein Air Painters
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 ABOUT THIS GROUP - PLEASE READ BEFORE ASKING TO JOIN. ABOUT THE GROUP This group is focused on the art of painting "plein air", outdoors in natural light. There are lots of other groups on Facebook where you can post works of various genre, but not here. OPEN TO PLEIN AIR PAINTERS This is a closed group, which means new members must be approved by the administrator. Membership is open to plein air artists, of any and all levels and mediums. This is a place to learn, make connections, share your experience, and perhaps sell a work. I encourage you to join! ADDING MEMERS: You may not add others to this group, they must request to join on their own. No one likes being added to a group w/out permission. It's SPAMy. POST PRE-REVIEWS Posts by new members are reviewed prior to posting. Inappropriate posts will not be posted, and the offending member removed from the group. We tightly control posts to keep this group focused on plein air painting and avoid SPAM. Please don't post more than 3 photos each day, unless you're capturing an event that requires more. Don't post images as downloads. This is to protect members from Malware. STUDIO WORK. It's fine to post studio work based on plein air, but you must first demonstrate that you're a plein air artist and a regular part of our community. To make it clear which of your work was done in the studio, please add the text "Studio work" somewhere in your post. I also encourage you to post plein air studies that inspired your studio work. POST YOUR WORK ONLY You may only post your own work. We don't want this to be place where galleries bombard us with the work of plein air artists they represent. REPORTING POSTS If you see a post that you suspect is SPAM or doesn't meet these guidelines, please use the top-right drop down menu for the post and "report it" to the Administrator. BE NICE If you feel a conversation in a post's comments are uncivil, attacking others, hateful, or harmful to the group, please bring it to my attention by reporting it, using the top-right drop down (arrow) menu for the post. WORKSHOPS &amp; EXHIBITIONS Group member painters who regularly post their work here are welcome to share their exhibitions or workshops, but please no more than 2 posts per event. Only artists who are members here may post these events, not galleries or workshop organizers. If you're not a painter but posting an event, or if you post looks like in advertisement--it will not be approved. We're keeping this group ad-free. EQUIPMENT Don't post stuff for sale. ADVERTISING If you use this group to advertise, you'll be removed. This is a place for plein air artists to share. If you want to reach members of the community, buy ads on Facebook or post content here that is relevant to them and meets these guidelines Thanks for participating, and I hope you enjoy the inspiring work and art posted here. Ed Terpening, Founder &amp; Administrator
                </div>
               </div>

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Technical Theatre Artists of L.A.
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 A forum for opportunities and resources for Los Angeles Technical Theatre Artists. All opportunities must post their offered dollar amount. For full-time positions, a range is sufficient. Postings that request applicants to inquire before declaring expected compensation will be deleted without warning. This is not a forum for advertising shows. We appreciate the hard work of all of our members, but promotional posts belong elsewhere. If you are applying to join, please offer ANY evidence on your profile that you are involved in theatre in any fashion, and live in Los Angeles.

User comments are not edited for accuracy or safety; however, to ensure a continually positive experience for the community, we may report or remove content or commentary containing spam, profanity, or otherwise objectionable or prohibited material.

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Year of the Stage Manager 2020/21
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 2020-June 2021 is the "year" to celebrate Stage Managers and educate people about what Stage Managers do! TO JOIN: Simply request to join with the purpose of celebrating Stage Managers and educating people about what we do. The purpose of the group is to foster conversation about stage management, advocacy for stage managers, and the sharing of resources. The goal is to be supportive of one another and approach topics with kindness, while assuming best intent. No advertising or other solicitation will be allowed in the group unless it is deemed apropos of the stage management and performing arts experience; you may post relevant job listings. Political campaigns germane to stage management and the performing arts industry are welcome and will be monitored at the discretion of the administrators and moderators. YSM2020/21 seeks to create space for candidates in an equitable fashion. You are 100% responsible for your own choices and posts in terms of disclosure/non-disclosure. If you wish to use any of the content of this board anywhere else, please ask permission of those involved in the discussion. Please credit authors, photographers, and content creators. We encourage you to acknowledge the source of a post, whether it be an individual or publication. Participants in the Year of the Stage Manager must include content and trigger warnings where applicable. Here is a helpful guide about using trigger warnings: https://www.oxfordsu.org/resourcehub/guidetotriggerwarnings/ YSM2020/21 does not tolerate hateful language and behavior. We value the idea that impact matters more than intent. Bullying of any kind isn't allowed, and degrading comments about things like race, religion, culture, sexual orientation, gender or identity will not be tolerated. There will be no singling out of any one participant and posts will be removed at the discretion of the administrators and moderators. While it’s expected there may be differences of opinion expressed from time to time, there will be zero tolerance for any attacks of a personal nature. You are welcome to disagree with a person’s point of view, but we will not permit disparagement or denigration of that person. The administrators and moderators reserve the right to enforce this policy as they see fit. Coercion, threats, blackmailing, and blacklisting are forms of aggressive and bullying behavior and will not be tolerated -- whether it is directed at members or administrators and moderators. This behavior will lead to expulsion from the group. These community guidelines are subject to change. The administrators and moderators will consider the removal of content and individuals that are reported; action will be taken at the full discretion of the administrators and moderators. DISCLAIMER: Actors' Equity Association does not monitor or take responsibility for the content, information, and views presented and represented here. The content of this group does not represent official positions
                </div>
               </div>

              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 AntiRacism Learning + Action Space for White People in U.S. Theatre
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 DESCRIPTION: This group is a resource-sharing and action hub for white people working in theatre in the U.S. who are committed to interrupting and dismantling systemic racism and anti-blackness, and advancing antiracism in their personal and professional lives. While the group is private, anyone who asks to join and agrees to the community guidelines will be admitted including Black, Indigenous, and People of Color (BIPOC). IMPORTANT: While this group is intended to be a space for white folks to share resources and engage in conversation around antiracist education and action, BIPOC members are joyfully welcomed in order to ensure accountability and to provide any feedback or comments they deem useful. No individual who wants to be involved will be denied entry (provided they agree to adhere to the community agreements upon requesting access). Members who consistently move against the community agreements will be removed from the group. Community agreements (FB's "Group Rules"): https://docs.google.com/document/d/1j7fcWzVO1SwWQRDOr4Bnyh9c6YpFxp7zzol1gn6J_jw/edit ALSO IMPORTANT: This is a group with a focus--to shift white people working in U.S. theatre toward antiracism and activate us to interrupt and dismantle systemic racism and anti-blackness. It’s a space to extend growing edge(s) and share tools for antiracist action. It isn’t a forum for posing questions that can be asked of your local community, other message boards, service organizations, or Google. It isn’t a place to promote your work or work you’re producing, or fundraise for an organization or cause. Please read the community agreements and contact a moderator if you have questions. AS YOU ENGAGE: We urge you to do so generously and urgently with respect to eradicating racism in our sector and country. None of us are experts, but that doesn't mean that we should hold back from effecting deep, lasting change. We will be courageous as we hold each other accountable to these agreements, not in order to shame but to strengthen our work together. IF ANTIRACISM WORK OR WHITE ANTIRACIST LEARNING SPACES ARE NEW TO YOU: We encourage you to explore these resources: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1uQZhwRMN6Z6RcdxYzudoZAPovSRGcaOYfYCvhWuOOt8/edit Also check out the group’s Foundational Terms &amp; Definitions: https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Xtc2J0sv3J0mT1P6pi8ozsgdxPYT-9hP9Oy5Y1jzAv0/edit?fbclid=IwAR35UaYfNFHuahfXJXTPGMBht2WlOiGa5EgMaWnlkNHcRyAkpSv9_zTYdvg *Please Note* Everything above is perpetually "in draft."

                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Landscape Artists -- Add ONLY 3 images at a time.
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                  Upon meeting so many incredibly great artists on Facebook, and noticing all the well executed landscape works, I realized there was not a group (at least none that I have noticed as of yet) dedicated to all landscape painters/artists no matter what media, whether they work plein air or in their studio, it doesn't matter. So, this group, and I hope it can be successful, is for all landscape painters, no matter who you are or where you are located... in America or Across the Seas. It is exciting that every day can bring another way of expressing and interpreting what we see and feel about the landscape before us. As nature continuously changes, we strive to capture and interpret her many moods, her essence, her ambiance, her soul. Through these landscape works, we can share her serenity and tranquility of what we feel about nature and to instill in the viewer a sense of her beauty and greatness...and the importance of preserving and taking care of all of nature for the sake of all life on this earth. This is truly what this group is all about. The preservation of the landscape...to open the viewers eyes to her. POST only up to 4 paintings per week. (Can post three in a grouping.)

                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 That's It, I'm inkshaming. (Actually Bad Tattoos)
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 If a tattoo isn't your personal style, you disagree with the placement (like if you say you like tattoos because you're super fucking hip! But God forbid someone have a face tattoo!), if you're only posting for attention, or if you're trying to get validation for a tattoo on you body that you know is fine... This isn't the place for you. If you're triggered by skin, and think every post should conform to your CW's... This isn't the place for you. This is a place to post truly awful, shitty tattoos, and laugh at them together. Any subject matter is welcome, your content warnings are not. Just don't be an asshole.

                <div class="_8um4">
                 <span class="_8ul_"><i class="_8wo5 _8wos img sp_oDRLRzjLfgY sx_8f3bf5"></i><span class="_8um1">10&nbsp;万位成员</span></span><span class="_8um0"><i class="_8wo6 _8wos img sp_oDRLRzjLfgY sx_ce40e2"></i><span class="_8um2">10 篇新帖</span></span>

             <div class="_8vrm">
              <a role="button" class="_42ft _8ugc _8x33 _8tjl _2ph-" aria-label="加入小组 That's It, I'm inkshaming. (Actually Bad Tattoos)" id="joinButton_1955567744662792" href="#" ajaxify="/ajax/timeline/sign_up_dialog/?next=https%3A%2F%2Fzh-cn.facebook.com%2Fgroups%2F1955567744662792%2F&amp;entity_id=1955567744662792&amp;context=join_group" rel="async-post">加入小组</a>
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="_8sz1 _8sz5 _8szd _8szj" id="u_0_8g">
            <div class="_8t03 _8tm_">
             <a class="_8ulx" href="/groups/959891544070003/">
              <div class="_8uly">
               <div class="_8wo2"></div>
              </div>
              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Traditional Oil Painting
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Discussions of traditional oil painting methods and materials and related matters, updated information for readers of Virgil Elliott's book, "Traditional Oil Painting - Advanced Techniques and Concepts from the Renaissance to the Present," Admin-approved announcements of exhibits, classes and workshops, et cetera. This group is essentially an extension of Virgil Elliott's book. As in the Cowdisley Group on Yahoo Groups, which is also moderated by Virgil Elliott, civility is a condition of participation. Personal disparagement is not acceptable behavior here. Address the points with which you disagree, not the personal aspects of the person who presented those points. That's how ethical debate is conducted, and I insist on it in this group. Posts that cross that line will be deleted. Discussions are in the English language. The rationale/philosophy behind this group may be summarized as essentially this: You never can know when something you paint is going to turn out to be really special, outstanding, inspiring, so it makes good sense to use the most lightfast pigments and most durable materials and workmanship with that possibility in mind. The longer a painting with a special quality with the power to inspire people in a positive way lasts and retains that quality, the more people it will be able to inspire. How many of us were inspired to become artists by seeing a centuries-old painting that moved us profoundly? Why not aspire to create that same kind of inspiration for people far into the future? Please DO NOT POST YOUR OWN WORK HERE for self-promotion or for critique. Post your work or works in progress if there is a point being illustrated that fits the mission of this group. I will also delete posts that contain bad information, so do your research before posting advice. This group is here to help people, and giving bad advice does not fit with that objective. Anyone who posts bad advice will be placed on Moderator Approval for all new posts. Facebook will only let me do that for 30 days at a time, otherwise I'd make it permanent or until I'm satisfied the problem will not return. If you are not sure your advice is true or good, please don't post it. There are people here who are experts who can provide reliable information based on sound knowledge, so the questions will get good answers. I'd rather the good answers not be in the minority, buried under a stack of bad ones that I'll have to correct or delete. Because I am currently writing a book to address the allegations that Johannes Vermeer worked with the aid of some optical device, I prohibit discussion of optical device theories in this group until after the book is published. To ignore this admonition will bring one brief warning, which if not heeded will result in immediate expulsion from this group. Members, please do not use Traditional Oil Painting to express your personal political or religious beliefs. There are other places where those topics can be discussed.
                </div>
               </div>

                 The All About Art and Artist (5A Club) is open to everyone worldwide who would like to display their quality art work. Thank you and enjoy the amazing talented artist paintings on the All About Art and Artist group.                 <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Ask A Professional Tattoo Artist
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                  -This is a place to ask questions about tattoos and have them answered by only the ADMINS of this group who are professional tattoo artists. It is NOT for ANYONE else to give advice or answer questions that are asked..ANY other unapproved suggestions or advice will be deleted. -If you have a simple question regarding an already posted topic you can comment in it HOWEVER if it is unrelated to the post or an elaborate question please make a new post and it will be answered separately. Please note that any answer or reply is not a substitute for advising your tattoo artist or doctor. -The group is growing more and more members every day...what that means is more and more comments are starting to fill the posts. Once 1 person comments a few other people comment..then a handful more. Before we know it the admins have to shift thru and delete 15 or 20 comments that are just complicating things. We now ask you DONT comment meaningless responses. -This is NOT the place to ask HOW TO tattoo. It is for advice about your tattoo, future tattoo or how/what to look for in a reputable tattoo artist near you. We don't refer to local shops but we will help you to understand what to look for in finding a good artist. Lastly, were humans who like to help but can be quite busy at times so we will help as soon as we can!

              <div class="_8uly">
               <div class="_8wo2"></div>
              </div>
              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Seascapes, Dunes, Marine and Coastal Painters-ONLY 3 at a time.
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 I order to join this group, please READ and AGREE to the Rules and Guidelines. Thank you. 1) ONLY post YOUR OWN seascape PAINTINGS, that YOU youself have created. Not the work of family, friends, collegues, etc. ~ NOTE: A 'painting' is the end product of the act of painting, i.e. the application of paints and/or pigments (and other media) to a surface, such as canvas, paper, panel, etc. Respectfully, this is not a forum for other arts or crafts, such a ceramics, sculpture, glass, etc. 2) Post a max. of THREE (3) images per DAY. Do NOT 'share' entire albums. Please Include title/size/media. Don't forget - please make your image viewable to all by setting it to 'PUBLIC'.. 3) All art work MUST relate to the subject matter of the group's name. i.e. MARINE PAINTINGS only, and be representational. ~ NO landscapes ~ NO rivers/ponds/lakes/waterfalls* ~ NO portraits ~ NO animals etc. ~ NO Abstracts ~ NO photographs, digitally enhanced or otherwise. Reference pics can be included where relevent. *'MARINE' specifically refers to salt water. Please check with admin if you have a 'Great Lakes' image you wish to share. Basically, WAVES, BEACH, DUNES will be your qualifiyng features, but please contact admin if you are unsure. 4) ALL images must be posted DIRECTLY to the group, or shared from your personal Facebook page. LINKS to your personal external website/blog can be added to YOUR post, or in the comments section beneath it. Please do not add links to another member's post. Please do NOT link directly or indirectly to any other external sites, such as Etsy, FineArtAmerica, eBay, etc. Do NOT link to external video sites, such as YouTube, Vimeo, etc. 5) Feel free to encourage, comment and ask questions. 6) Snide/derogatory comments will NOT BE TOLERATED. Offenders will find themselves slung overboard, no questions asked. 7) DO NOT post photos/images or insert external links into the comments section of another members post, unless asked for. They will be deleted. 8) You may post photos of your art studios or plein air painting photos. Got a seascape exhibition coming up? Created a seascape Facebook event? Tell us about it! NOTE: Please remember that you have control of your own posts. If there is a comment that you don't care for, you have the ability to 'Hide' 'Report' or even 'Block' the offending comment or its originator. NOTE: So long as you keep within the above guidelines, you can include a price if your painting is available for sale. HOWEVER, please realise that this is probably not an ideal venue to directly market your work. FINAL NOTE: In order to avoid ambiguity and retain fairness, Admin reserves the right to remove deviations from the above guidelines at its discretion. With ALL of that out of the way, WELCOME, and THANK YOU so much for supporting this WONDERFUL group! 
                </div>

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 ARCHITECTURE
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Architecture (Latin architectura, from the Greek ἀρχιτέκτων – arkhitekton, from ἀρχι- "chief" and τέκτων "builder, carpenter, mason") can mean: The art and science of designing and erecting buildings and other physical structures. The practice of an architect, where architecture means to offer or render professional services in connection with the design and construction of a building, or group of buildings and the space within the site surrounding the buildings, that have as their principal purpose human occupancy or use.[1] A general term to describe buildings and other structures. A style and method of design and construction of buildings and other physical structures. A wider definition may comprise all design activity, from the macro-level (urban design, landscape architecture) to the micro-level (construction details and furniture). Architecture is both the process and product of planning, designing and constructing form, space and ambience that reflect functional, technical, social, and aesthetic considerations. It requires the creative manipulation and coordination of material, technology, light and shadow. Architecture also encompasses the pragmatic aspects of realizing buildings and structures, including scheduling, cost estimating and construction administration. As documentation produced by architects, typically drawings, plans and technical specifications, architecture defines the structure and/or behavior of a building or any other kind of system that is to be or has been constructed. Architectural works are often perceived as cultural and political symbols and as works of art. Historical civilizations are often identified with their surviving architectural achievements. Architecture sometimes refers to the activity of designing any kind of system and the term is common in the information technology world. Theory of architecture Main article: Architectural theory [edit]Historic treatises The Parthenon, Athens, Greece, "the supreme example among architectural sites." (Fletcher).[2] The earliest surviving written work on the subject of architecture is De architectura, by the Roman architect Vitruvius in the early 1st century CE.[3] According to Vitruvius, a good building should satisfy the three principles of firmitas, utilitas, venustas,[4][5] which translate roughly as - Durability - it should stand up robustly and remain in good condition. Utility - it should be useful and function well for the people using it Beauty - it should delight people and raise their spirits. According to Vitruvius, the architect should strive to fulfill each of these three attributes as well as possible. Leone Battista Alberti, who elaborates on the ideas of Vitruvius in his treatise, De Re Aedificatoria, saw beauty primarily as a matter of proportion, although ornament also played a part. For Alberti, the rules of proportion were those that governed the idealised human figure, the Golden mean. The most important aspect of beauty was therefore an inherent part of an object, rather than something applied superficially; and was based on universal, recognisable truths. The notion of style in the arts was not developed until the 16th century, with the writing of Vasari.[6] The treatises, by the 18th century, had been translated into Italian, French, Spanish and English. Unite d'Habitation by Le Corbusier at Briey, France In the early nineteenth century, Augustus Welby Northmore Pugin wrote Contrasts (1836) that, as the titled suggested, contrasted the modern, industrial world, which he disparaged, with an idealized image of neo-medieval world. Gothic architecture, Pugin believed, was the only “true Christian form of architecture.” The 19th century English art critic, John Ruskin, in his Seven Lamps of Architecture, published 1849,[7] was much narrower in his view of what constituted architecture. Architecture was the "art which so disposes and adorns the edifices raised by men ... that the sight of them" contributes "to his mental health, power, and pleasure". For Ruskin, the aesthetic was of overriding significance. His work goes on to state that a building is not truly a work of architecture unless it is in some way "adorned". For Ruskin, a well-constructed, well-proportioned, functional building needed string courses or rustication, at the very least. On the difference between the ideals of "architecture" and mere "construction", the renowned 20th C. architect Le Corbusier wrote: "You employ stone, wood, and concrete, and with these materials you build houses and palaces: that is construction. Ingenuity is at work. But suddenly you touch my heart, you do me good. I am happy and I say: This is beautiful. That is Architecture".[8] The National Congress of Brazil, designed by Oscar Niemeyer. [edit]Modern concepts of architecture The great 19th century architect of skyscrapers, Louis Sullivan, promoted an overriding precept to architectural design: "Form follows function". While the notion that structural and aesthetic considerations should be entirely subject to functionality was met with both popularity and skepticism, it had the effect of introducing the concept of "function" in place of Vitruvius' "utility". "Function" came to be seen as encompassing all criteria of the use, perception and enjoyment of a building, not only practical but also aesthetic, psychological and cultural. Sydney Opera House, Australia designed by Utzon. Nunzia Rondanini stated, "Through its aesthetic dimension architecture goes beyond the functional aspects that it has in common with other human sciences. Through its own particular way of expressing values, architecture can stimulate and influence social life without presuming that, in and of itself, it will promote social development.' To restrict the meaning of (architectural) formalism to art for art's sake is not only reactionary; it can also be a purposeless quest for perfection or originality which degrades form into a mere instrumentality".[9] Among the philosophies that have influenced modern architects and their approach to building design are rationalism, empiricism, structuralism, poststructuralism, and phenomenology. In the late 20th century a new concept was added to those included in the compass of both structure and function, the consideration of sustainability. To satisfy the contemporary ethos a building should be constructed in a manner which is environmentally friendly in terms of the production of its materials, its impact upon the natural and built environment of its surrounding area and the demands that it makes upon non-sustainable power sources for heating, cooling, water and waste management and lighting. [edit]

                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Hi folks First of all, welcome to everybody, old and new members, artists and fans. We are growing fast, so I gave it up to welcome all new members personally, but if you like you can share a link to your main site and maybe say a bit about yourself? No obligation, if you have nothing to share at the moment, well, just sit back, relax and watch. Please feel free to invite your friends. Main focus of this group is streetart and everything related. We all love street art and some of us post a lot on several social media platforms. We exchange the best pics and interact with the artists. Here we offer a platform for some self-promotion, information about upcoming events or general discussion about streetart related things. Share your best pictures, and honour the artist and the photographer (if possible). This group started as an accompanying group for the community group on Pinterest "Street art (Best of) - Community Edition" https://www.pinterest.com/weigeltw/street-art-best-of-community-edition/ , come take a look, we have tons of pictures.                  Pure Watercolors for Beginners
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 NOTE TO those painters wanting to join us: Make sure to answer all questions when you request to join. Welcome to Pure Watercolors! This is a community of watercolor lovers, from total beginners to slightly more experienced, and even though with more! It is a place to post your work, learn from each other, share helpful tips and tricks, get encouragement or ask for pointers. Only posts about watercolor art, no advertisements, no selling, and no other forms of art will be allowed. Please keep discussions and art clean and respectful. No foul language, vulgarity, hate speech or politics will be allowed. Thank you and enjoy painting together!

                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Watercolour Techniques and Tips
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Welcome to all! This group is for the sharing and discussion of techniques for painting with watercolours. GUIDELINES - PLEASE READ! 1. Post only once a day, directly into the group 2. Share DETAILS of a technique or tip OR ask a specific question about technique 3. Include up to 5 images to illustrate your tip or technique in the main post, if you wish 4. Comply with copyright law 5. Give credit to the photographer or the artist who has inspired you 6. Play nicely Please come back later and read more details below if you're not sure, or ask an admin for help. WE DO NOT ALLOW: Showcasing of your work - post instead to Simply Watercolour Group General descriptions or requests for critique Copies of tutorials or other artwork Direct or indirect advertising, links to websites, ‘Like page’ buttons, hashtags or any other promotions Posts that are shared from your page or album Offensive language, behaviour or images. MORE INFORMATION 1. POST ONLY ONCE A DAY, as text, text with explanatory photos, or short videos, directly into the group ie in the box where it says "Write something ...". Please PUT A SHORT DESCRIPTIVE TOPIC TITLE AT THE BEGINNING OF YOUR TEXT so that searching for topics will be easier. 2. SHARE A TIP OR TECHNIQUE Give details. Posts that just describe eg I used salt, will be deleted. Tell us how you used the salt, how thick or thin your paint was, your reasons for choosing those colours. Specific questions should invite discussion about technique rather than ask for critique 3. INCLUDE UP TO 5 IMAGES that illustrate your tip or question in the main post. Video can be shared to explain your tip or technique. It must be your own educational video tutorial that specifically explains the technique. Generic painting demonstrations and any video not accompanied by a written explanation will be deleted. If the video is already on YouTube please direct members to look there. 4. COMPLY WITH COPYRIGHT LAW. Use only your own ORIGINAL work, work you have permission from the artist/originator to share or anything covered by a creative commons licence. Other material will be deleted by the admin team. PLEASE NOTE WE ARE NO LONGER ACCEPTING COPIES OF TUTORIALS IN THIS GROUP. Facebook copyright help page: https://www.facebook.com/help/1020633957973118… 5. GIVE CREDIT to the photographer or the artist who has inspired you to try the technique you are sharing eg in the style of Anne Artiste 6. PLAY NICELY - Please be positive with comments. If people want help, they will ask. All posts are subject to the approval of the admins Admins may turn off comments or delete a post at any time if necessary. Members who block, attack or insult the admins will be deleted from the page and blocked. 
                </div>
               </div>

              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Save the Heritages of Bangladesh
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Architecture that enriches experience, strengthens cultural diversity, innovation and space, is to be conserved for stewardship and scholarship as a symbol of cultural identity and continuity. As a means of preserving heritage, it is significant to a society that values its roots, and wants to learn about its achievements at a point in history. Bangladesh, heir to rich architecture spanning over two millennia, possesses many settlements and buildings of cultural significance that are to be held in trust for the future generation catering for the emotional insecurity perpetuated by rapid changes. This entails a high degree of moral commitment and positive optimism in humanity and its future. While many nations are active in preserving built heritage, historic towns and cultural landscapes, institutional and socio-economic conditions have inhibited this in Bangladesh. Scrupulous forces of urbanisation and commercial interest have fostered an environment where the treasure and wisdom in traditional architecture is treated with disdain. Such lack of awareness has become the greatest threat to the survival of these treasure troves. This page aims to raise awareness among people from all strata of society about the rich architectural heritage of Bangladesh through various means.
                </div>
               </div>

                <div class="_8um4">

              <div class="_8tn0">
               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 21st Century Glass : Conversations and Images / Glass Secessionism
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 The intent of this group is to underscore and appreciate glass sculptural art in the 21st Century and to illustrate the differences and strengths compared to late 20th century technique-driven glass. While the 20th century glass artists contributions have been spectacular and ground breaking, this group focuses on the aesthetic of the 21st century. The object of the Glass-Secession is to advance glass as applied to sculptural expression; to draw together those glass artists practicing or otherwise interested in the arts, and to discuss from time to time examples of the Glass-Secession or other narrative work. This movement is modeled after Alfred Stieglitz and the Photo-Secessionists and how they redefined photography. It was said of Stieglitz: "What, then, was this secession from? It was not only from artwork that had gone stale through the copying of Victorian, conventional styles, but more importantly from the dictatorship of the entrenched institutions, galleries, art schools and professional art organizations that enforced or at very least sanctioned copying or imitation." Members are encouraged to post and share examples of 21st century glass sculpture and open discussion topics regarding this issue. Please do not self promote, but feel free to show others work. Please do not post notices for position openings, and we would appreciate if you would contact an administrator before posting notices for conferences or calls for papers. We ask that members keep topics focused by thread. Do not start a new thread when posting on an existing thread with similar subject matter will suffice. Here is a link to the full article dealing with Glass Secessionism. http://washingtonglass.blogspot.com/2013/07/glass-secessionism.html 
                </div>
               </div>

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Los Angeles Art Opportunities
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 This is a group for Los Angeles-area visual artists and those who can provide them opportunities. The goal is to strengthen the Los Angeles-area art community through the sharing of opportunities. Please post: - Job listings for artists - Calls for art - Artist studio/housing for rent - Announcements about fine art classes - Lectures for artists - Free art items - Tips for being a successful artist - Auditions, but only if specifically for visual artists Please do NOT post: - Show/event announcements - Art or art items for sale - Kickstarter or other fund-raising efforts - Self-promotional or friend-promotional content, including images of art Questions to the group will be posted on a case-by-case basis, and only if they are applicable to a broad range of artists and haven't been discussed recently. People who are rude, disrespectful or disregard these guidelines will be removed from the group. Installation artist Dani Dodge is the Founder and Moderator of Los Angeles Art Opportunities.

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Painting Tips and Julie McDowell and Friends
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 PLEASE READ This page is about painting furniture and having fun The dreaded rules We have to have some rules as we grow! 1. Be kind and respectful. This group is above all else about kindness and sharing 2. Please show before and after pictures of your masterpieces. 3. Share how you achieved your finish, with paint colours and brands etc. in the original post. If this is not included, sorry, the post will be deleted 4. Ask questions about painting furniture and prep. 5. No links to other groups, please. 6. No advertising, please, do not link to retailer sites without checking with admin. 7. Please post directly to the page and not from a business page. 8. Any questions about the rules, message one of the admins or moderators. We have 3 moderators Cindy Ward Nehlsen, Marijana Kuljis and Deirdre Riggall-Service. We all have a badge next to our names. 9. Many questions have been answered, use the search bar with the keywords to find past posts 10. Please get 'admin approval' to post videos and blogs. We have to be able to verify the information before sharing it. 11. We have an IG page and will be sharing work from this page. If this is NOT ok, please let an admin know 12. Have fun! There is a lot of information on the page and people's experiences, as always it is important that you verify for yourself how to use a product if unsure go to the manufacturer's website! This group belongs to us all, share ideas, post questions and techniques but most of all please be kind to one another. With love' The Admin Team xoxo

                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Theatre Nerds Backstage
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 We are thespians! A safe place for theatre nerds to be theatre nerds. Share stories, ask/receive advice, tips, etc. Network with fellow actors, techies &amp; creatives in the theatrical community. This group's main purpose is to help and encourage each other... and the theatre nerd community. Having a group makes it easier to connect individually. We want this to be a safe space for you to ask questions &amp; give input in regards to making TN a better platform. Some group do's and don'ts DO: -Help each other -Give constructive criticism (emphases on constructive) -Post about the shows your in, working on, etc. -Ask advice -Treat each other with respect -Treat everyone equally with love -Share audition ideas, etc. -Post meme's &amp; videos DON'T: -Post bootlegs -Promote your own or someone else's personal blog, facebook page, etc. (unless permission is given) -Call people names -Try and sell anything or crowd funding (unless given permission so ask first) Welcome to this amazing community everyone! Don't hesitate to ask me any questions! -Ben

               <div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8s__ fsm">
                 Bauhaus Movement
                </div>
                <div class="mvm uiP _8t00 fsm">
                 Rethinking the world. Learn how the Bauhaus influenced design history with its emphasis on theory and practice as taught by the masters. For many artists, architects and designers, the Bauhaus was an ideology and a conviction, not just a school of arts and architecture. Experimenting with new materials and forms entailed a whole new living environment. Bauhaus existed from 1919 to 1933 and today the world considers it to be the home of the avant-guard of classical modern style in all fields of liberal and applied arts.
                </div>
               </div>
               <div>
                <div class="_8um4">

             <h2 class="_8tjp _8usa _8us0 _8us1">小组和隐私设置</h2>
             <div class="mvm uiP _8tjq fsm">
              你可以公开分享小组，也可设为仅对成员可见。我们的隐私设置让你能把小组分享给指定对象。
             </div><a role="button" class="_42ft _8ugc _8x33 _8tjm _2pi6 _8tjn" href="/community/using-key-groups-tools/understanding-your-privacy-settings/">详细了解</a>
